To preprocess your data by normalizing the usage_amount field and storing it as a new file, I will write a script that reads your data, normalizes the usage_amount values, and saves the resulting DataFrame to a new CSV file.

Here's the Python script to achieve this:

python
Copy code
import pandas as pd
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler

# Load the data
data_path = "./your_data.csv"  # Update this path to your actual data file location
df = pd.read_csv(data_path)

# Initialize the MinMaxScaler
scaler = MinMaxScaler()

# Normalize the usage_amount column
df['normalized_usage_amount'] = scaler.fit_transform(df[['usage_amount']])

# Save the preprocessed data to a new file
output_path = "./SRC/data/split_data/normalized_data.csv"
df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)

print(f"Normalized data saved to {output_path}")
Steps:
Read the Data: The script reads the CSV file containing your data.
Normalize: The usage_amount field is normalized using the MinMaxScaler from sklearn.preprocessing.
Save the Data: The normalized data is saved as a new CSV file in the specified directory.
Note:
Update the data_path to the location where your original data file is stored.
The output_path is where the normalized data will be saved. You can adjust it based on your directory structure.
After running this script, you'll find the normalized data stored in the specified directory.

ChatGPT said:
ChatGPT
I've revised your code to ensure it works correctly. Here's the fixed version:

python
Copy code
import matplotlib.pyplot as plot
import numpy as np
import scipy.stats as stats
import pandas as pd
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler

# Read the list of service fields
fields = list(pd.read_csv("./SRC/data/split_data/_Services.csv"))

# Loop through the last element of the fields list (as per your original code)
for i in range(len(fields)-1, len(fields)):
    path = "./SRC/data/split_data/" + fields[i] + ".csv"  # Use the correct index i
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    z_scores = []

    # Calculate z-scores for each chunk of the data
    for j in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (j - 1))
        post = int(n * j)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        z_scores.extend(zstat)  # Collect z-scores for the entire data

    # Insert z-scores into the DataFrame
    df.insert(4, "z_score", z_scores)

    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()

    # Normalize the usage_amount column
    df['normalized_usage_amount'] = scaler.fit_transform(df[['usage_amount']])

    # Plot the data
    figure, axis = plot.subplots(3, 1, figsize=(10, 8))  # Adjusted subplot layout
    x1 = df["usage_end_time"]
    y1 = df["cost"]
    y2 = df["z_score"]
    y3 = df["normalized_usage_amount"]

    axis[0].plot(x1, y1)
    axis[0].set_title("Cost over Time")
    axis[0].set_xlabel("Time")
    axis[0].set_ylabel("Cost")

    axis[1].plot(x1, y2, color="red")
    axis[1].set_title("Z-Score of Usage Amount over Time")
    axis[1].set_xlabel("Time")
    axis[1].set_ylabel("Z-Score")

    axis[2].plot(x1, y3)
    axis[2].set_title("Normalized Usage Amount over Time")
    axis[2].set_xlabel("Time")
    axis[2].set_ylabel("Normalized Usage Amount")

    plot.tight_layout()
    plot.show()
Explanation of Changes:
Indexing Correction: I corrected the indexing when accessing fields[i].
Normalized Usage Amount: Normalization is applied to the entire usage_amount column after calculating z-scores, and the normalized values are stored in the new column normalized_usage_amount.
Subplots Layout: Adjusted the layout to ensure plots are clear and non-overlapping.
Plot Titles and Labels: Added titles and labels to each subplot for better clarity.
Steps to Run:
Ensure the path "./SRC/data/split_data/_Services.csv" is correct and accessible.
This script will read the last CSV file listed in _Services.csv, process it, and then plot the required fields.
Let me know if you need any further adjustments!

ChatGPT said:
ChatGPT
Here’s the modified code to normalize the z-scores instead of the usage_amount:

python
Copy code
import matplotlib.pyplot as plot
import numpy as np
import scipy.stats as stats
import pandas as pd
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler

# Read the list of service fields
fields = list(pd.read_csv("./SRC/data/split_data/_Services.csv"))

# Loop through the list of service fields
for i in range(1, len(fields)):
    path = "./SRC/data/split_data/" + fields[i] + ".csv"  # Use the correct index i
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    z_scores = []

    # Calculate z-scores for each chunk of the data
    for j in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (j - 1))
        post = int(n * j)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        z_scores.extend(zstat)  # Collect z-scores for the entire data

    # Insert z-scores into the DataFrame
    df.insert(4, "z_score", z_scores)

    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()

    # Normalize the z_score column
    df['normalized_z_score'] = scaler.fit_transform(df[['z_score']])

    # Plot the data
    figure, axis = plot.subplots(3, 1, figsize=(10, 8))  # Adjusted subplot layout
    x1 = df["usage_end_time"]
    y1 = df["cost"]
    y2 = df["normalized_z_score"]
    y3 = df["usage_amount"]

    axis[0].plot(x1, y1)
    axis[0].set_title("Cost over Time")
    axis[0].set_xlabel("Time")
    axis[0].set_ylabel("Cost")

    axis[1].plot(x1, y2, color="red")
    axis[1].set_title("Normalized Z-Score of Usage Amount over Time")
    axis[1].set_xlabel("Time")
    axis[1].set_ylabel("Normalized Z-Score")

    axis[2].plot(x1, y3)
    axis[2].set_title("Usage Amount over Time")
    axis[2].set_xlabel("Time")
    axis[2].set_ylabel("Usage Amount")

    plot.tight_layout()
    plot.show()
Changes:
Normalization of z_score: I replaced the normalization of usage_amount with the normalization of the z_score values.
Column Name: The normalized z-scores are stored in a new column called normalized_z_score.
Output:
The plots will show:
Cost over time.
Normalized Z-Score over time.
Usage Amount over time.
Let me know if you need any further adjustments!

ChatGPT said:
ChatGPT
Here’s how you can modify the addZscore function to normalize the z_score column after it's created:

python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import matplotlib.pyplot as plot

def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Insert the z-scores into the DataFrame
    df.insert(4, "z_score", fin)
    
    # Normalize the z_score column
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    df['normalized_z_score'] = scaler.fit_transform(df[['z_score']])
    
    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

    # Uncomment the plotting section if you want to visualize the results
    # figure, axis = plot.subplots(3)
    # x1 = df["usage_end_time"]
    # y1 = df["cost"]
    # y2 = df["normalized_z_score"]
    # y3 = df["usage_amount"]
    # axis[0].plot(x1, y1)
    # axis[1].plot(x1, y2, c="red")
    # axis[2].plot(x1, y3)
    # plot.show()

# Example usage:
# addZscore("your_file_path.csv")
Explanation:
Normalization: After calculating the z-scores, the MinMaxScaler is applied to the z_score column to normalize it. The result is stored in a new column called normalized_z_score.
Saving Data: The DataFrame is saved back to the CSV file after normalization, without changing the original file path.
Plotting (Optional): The plotting part is commented out but can be uncommented if you wish to visualize the data.
You can now use this addZscore function to calculate and normalize the z-scores in your data.





You said:
from the code above can you please make it to that the unnormalized z score is not stored in the dataframe and csv
ChatGPT said:
ChatGPT
Certainly! Here's the updated addZscore function where only the normalized z-scores are stored in the DataFrame and CSV file:

python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import matplotlib.pyplot as plot

def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler and normalize z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert only the normalized z-scores into the DataFrame
    df.insert(4, "normalized_z_score", normalized_z_scores)

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

    # Uncomment the plotting section if you want to visualize the results
    # figure, axis = plot.subplots(3)
    # x1 = df["usage_end_time"]
    # y1 = df["cost"]
    # y2 = df["normalized_z_score"]
    # y3 = df["usage_amount"]
    # axis[0].plot(x1, y1)
    # axis[1].plot(x1, y2, c="red")
    # axis[2].plot(x1, y3)
    # plot.show()

# Example usage:
# addZscore("your_file_path.csv")
Changes Made:
Normalization and Storage: The unnormalized z-scores are normalized directly without being stored in the DataFrame. Only the normalized z-scores are stored in a new column, normalized_z_score.
CSV Export: When saving the DataFrame back to the CSV, it contains only the normalized z-scores along with the other original data.
Now, when you run the addZscore function, it will add only the normalized z-scores to the DataFrame and CSV file.

"import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import matplotlib.pyplot as plot

def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler and normalize z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert only the normalized z-scores into the DataFrame
    df.insert(4, "normalized_z_score", normalized_z_scores)

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)"

"import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data
data = pd.read_csv(r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv")
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time')
sequence_length = 10
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time'])

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Define a threshold for detecting spikes (e.g., 2 standard deviations from the mean of predictions)
threshold = 2 * np.std(y_full_pred)

def detect_spikes(predictions, threshold):
    spikes = []
    for i in range(len(predictions)):
        if predictions[i] > threshold:
            spikes.append(i)
    return spikes

# Detect spikes in the full dataset predictions
spike_indices = detect_spikes(y_full_pred, threshold)
print(f"Spikes detected at indices: {spike_indices}")

# Plot the results with spikes highlighted
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount (Full Dataset)')
plt.plot(y_full_pred, color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount (Full Dataset)')
plt.scatter(spike_indices, y_full_pred[spike_indices], color='green', marker='x', label='Detected Spikes')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted (Entire Dataset) with Spike Detection')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Usage Amount')
plt.legend()
plt.show()

if spike_indices:
    print(f"Warning: {len(spike_indices)} usage spikes detected!")
    # You could add more sophisticated alert mechanisms here, like sending an email or logging the event.
else:
    print("No usage spikes detected.")

ChatGPT said:
ChatGPT
Memory updated
To combine the data created from both the z-score method and the LSTM model for optimal forecast detection, you can integrate the z-score as an additional feature in the LSTM model. This approach allows the LSTM model to leverage the information provided by the z-scores, which could enhance its ability to detect anomalies or forecast more accurately.

Here’s how you can combine the two models:

1. Modify the addZscore Function:
First, ensure the addZscore function generates the normalized z-scores and stores them in a CSV file that will be used as input to the LSTM model.

2. Update the LSTM Model Code:
Next, modify the LSTM model code to include the normalized_z_score as an additional feature.

Combined Code Implementation:
python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Function to add z-score and normalize it
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Normalize the z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert normalized z-scores into the DataFrame
    df['normalized_z_score'] = normalized_z_scores

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

# Example usage to preprocess the data and add z-scores
z_score_data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
addZscore(z_score_data_path)

# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data with normalized z-scores
data = pd.read_csv(z_score_data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time')
sequence_length = 10
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time'])

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

# Create sequences including both usage_amount and normalized_z_score
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Define a threshold for detecting spikes (e.g., 2 standard deviations from the mean of predictions)
threshold = 2 * np.std(y_full_pred)

def detect_spikes(predictions, threshold):
    spikes = []
    for i in range(len(predictions)):
        if predictions[i] > threshold:
            spikes.append(i)
    return spikes

# Detect spikes in the full dataset predictions
spike_indices = detect_spikes(y_full_pred, threshold)
print(f"Spikes detected at indices: {spike_indices}")

# Plot the results with spikes highlighted
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount (Full Dataset)')
plt.plot(y_full_pred, color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount (Full Dataset)')
plt.scatter(spike_indices, y_full_pred[spike_indices], color='green', marker='x', label='Detected Spikes')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted (Entire Dataset) with Spike Detection')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Usage Amount')
plt.legend()
plt.show()

if spike_indices:
    print(f"Warning: {len(spike_indices)} usage spikes detected!")
    # You could add more sophisticated alert mechanisms here, like sending an email or logging the event.
else:
    print("No usage spikes detected.")
Summary of Changes:
Z-Score Normalization: The addZscore function calculates and normalizes the z-scores, which are then added to the dataset as a new column, normalized_z_score.
LSTM Input Modification: The LSTM model input now includes both the usage_amount and normalized_z_score as features, enhancing the model's ability to detect anomalies.
Spike Detection: The LSTM model’s predictions are used to detect spikes, potentially improved by the additional z-score feature.
This approach combines both statistical and machine learning methods to improve anomaly detection, making the forecasting more robust.

The error you're encountering is related to a mismatch in the dimensions of the input data and the expected input shape of the LSTM model. Specifically, the model is expecting inputs of one shape, but the data you're passing has a different number of features.

Likely Causes:
Input Shape Mismatch: The LSTM model was likely trained on a dataset with a different number of features. In your case, the LSTM model expects an input shape of (batch_size, sequence_length, 7), but you're providing an input with shape (batch_size, sequence_length, 8).

Feature Addition: When you added the normalized_z_score as a new feature, the number of features in the input data increased by one, which is causing the mismatch.

Solutions:
Option 1: Adjust the LSTM Model to Accept the Additional Feature
If you want to include the normalized_z_score as an additional feature, you'll need to adjust the LSTM model to accept the new input shape. This typically involves retraining the model with the new feature included.

Option 2: Remove a Feature or Combine Features
If you can't retrain the model, another option is to remove one of the features to match the original number of features that the model was trained on. For example, if your LSTM was originally trained with 7 features, you could drop one of the features in the input data before passing it to the model.

Here's how you can modify the code to match the original input shape:

python
Copy code
# Assuming the original model was trained on 7 features, drop one feature to match
# For example, dropping the 'normalized_z_score' feature

sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time', 'normalized_z_score'])  # Drop the normalized_z_score column

# Create sequences excluding the 'normalized_z_score'
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Proceed with predictions
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
Next Steps:
Retraining the Model: If possible, retrain your LSTM model using the dataset that includes the normalized_z_score feature. This way, the model will learn to work with the new input shape (sequence_length, 8).

Dropping Features: If retraining is not an option, consider dropping one of the features (like normalized_z_score) and using only the original features the model was trained on.

This should resolve the dimensional mismatch error you're encountering. Let me know if you need further assistance!

"import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Function to add z-score and normalize it
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Normalize the z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert normalized z-scores into the DataFrame
    df['normalized_z_score'] = normalized_z_scores

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

# Example usage to preprocess the data and add z-scores
z_score_data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
addZscore(z_score_data_path)

# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data with normalized z-scores
data = pd.read_csv(z_score_data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time')
sequence_length = 10
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time'])

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

# Create sequences including both usage_amount and normalized_z_score
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Define a threshold for detecting spikes (e.g., 2 standard deviations from the mean of predictions)
threshold = 2 * np.std(y_full_pred)

def detect_spikes(predictions, threshold):
    spikes = []
    for i in range(len(predictions)):
        if predictions[i] > threshold:
            spikes.append(i)
    return spikes

# Detect spikes in the full dataset predictions
spike_indices = detect_spikes(y_full_pred, threshold)
print(f"Spikes detected at indices: {spike_indices}")

# Plot the results with spikes highlighted
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount (Full Dataset)')
plt.plot(y_full_pred, color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount (Full Dataset)')
plt.scatter(spike_indices, y_full_pred[spike_indices], color='green', marker='x', label='Detected Spikes')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted (Entire Dataset) with Spike Detection')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Usage Amount')
plt.legend()
plt.show()

if spike_indices:
    print(f"Warning: {len(spike_indices)} usage spikes detected!")
    # You could add more sophisticated alert mechanisms here, like sending an email or logging the event.
else:
    print("No usage spikes detected.")

Here's the full code with adjustments to avoid the dimension mismatch error by dropping the normalized_z_score column, which allows the input to match the model's expected input shape:

python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Function to add z-score and normalize it
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Normalize the z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert normalized z-scores into the DataFrame
    df['normalized_z_score'] = normalized_z_scores

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

# Example usage to preprocess the data and add z-scores
z_score_data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
addZscore(z_score_data_path)

# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data with normalized z-scores
data = pd.read_csv(z_score_data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time' and 'normalized_z_score' to match model input)
sequence_length = 10
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time', 'normalized_z_score'])  # Drop the normalized_z_score column

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

# Create sequences
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Define a threshold for detecting spikes (e.g., 2 standard deviations from the mean of predictions)
threshold = 2 * np.std(y_full_pred)

def detect_spikes(predictions, threshold):
    spikes = []
    for i in range(len(predictions)):
        if predictions[i] > threshold:
            spikes.append(i)
    return spikes

# Detect spikes in the full dataset predictions
spike_indices = detect_spikes(y_full_pred, threshold)
print(f"Spikes detected at indices: {spike_indices}")

# Plot the results with spikes highlighted
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount (Full Dataset)')
plt.plot(y_full_pred, color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount (Full Dataset)')
plt.scatter(spike_indices, y_full_pred[spike_indices], color='green', marker='x', label='Detected Spikes')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted (Entire Dataset) with Spike Detection')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Usage Amount')
plt.legend()
plt.show()

if spike_indices:
    print(f"Warning: {len(spike_indices)} usage spikes detected!")
    # You could add more sophisticated alert mechanisms here, like sending an email or logging the event.
else:
    print("No usage spikes detected.")
Key Points:
Dropping normalized_z_score: The normalized_z_score column is dropped from the input data before feeding it into the LSTM model. This ensures that the input dimensions match what the model was originally trained on.
Maintaining Compatibility: By aligning the features with the model’s expectations, you avoid the dimension mismatch error that was previously encountered.
Flexibility: If you retrain the model in the future, you can reintroduce the normalized_z_score as a feature by adjusting the model architecture accordingly.
Running this code should work without any dimensional mismatch issues. Let me know if you encounter any further problems or have additional questions!

Certainly! Here's the modified code that creates a CSV file containing the predictions for the full data list, normalized to the predicted values.

Code:
python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import tensorflow as tf
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model

# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data
data = pd.read_csv(r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv")
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time')
sequence_length = 10
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time'])

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Normalize the predictions
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(y_full_pred)

# Combine actual values and predictions into a DataFrame
results_df = pd.DataFrame({
    'Actual_Usage_Amount': y,
    'Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred_normalized.flatten()
})

# Save the results to a CSV file
output_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\predictions.csv"
results_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)
print(f"Predictions saved to {output_path}")

# Optional: plot the actual vs predicted values
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred, color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred_normalized, color='orange', label='Normalized Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted (Full Dataset)')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Usage Amount')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Explanation:
Data Preparation: The create_sequences function generates sequences of data that are used as input for the LSTM model.
Prediction: The LSTM model makes predictions on the prepared sequences.
Normalization: The predictions (y_full_pred) are normalized using MinMaxScaler.
Results Saving: The actual usage amounts, predicted usage amounts, and normalized predicted usage amounts are saved into a CSV file.
Plotting (Optional): A plot is generated to visualize the actual vs. predicted usage amounts, including the normalized predictions.
Output:
CSV File: The results are saved in a CSV file located at the specified output_path.
Plot: The plot shows the actual usage amounts, predicted usage amounts, and normalized predicted usage amounts.
This code should produce a CSV file with the required predictions, and the plot will help you visualize the performance of your LSTM model.

The error you're encountering is related to a mismatch between the expected input shape for the LSTM model and the actual shape of the input data you're providing. Specifically, your LSTM model was trained with 7 features, but your input data has 8 features, leading to the mismatch.

To fix this, you need to ensure that the input data provided to the model matches the shape that the model was trained on. If your model was trained with 7 features, you should drop one of the features from the input data before feeding it into the model.

python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import tensorflow as tf
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model

# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data
data = pd.read_csv(r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv")
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time' and one additional column to match the model's expected input shape)
# Assume we need to drop the 'normalized_z_score' column to match the model's expected input shape
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time', 'normalized_z_score'])  # Drop 'normalized_z_score'

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

sequence_length = 10
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Normalize the predictions
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(y_full_pred)

# Combine actual values and predictions into a DataFrame
results_df = pd.DataFrame({
    'Actual_Usage_Amount': y,
    'Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred_normalized.flatten()
})

# Save the results to a CSV file
output_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\predictions.csv"
results_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)
print(f"Predictions saved to {output_path}")

# Optional: plot the actual vs predicted values
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred, color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred_normalized, color='orange', label='Normalized Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted (Full Dataset)')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Usage Amount')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Explanation:
Dropping the Extra Feature: The code now explicitly drops the normalized_z_score column before creating the sequences, ensuring that the input to the LSTM model matches the shape it was trained on (7 features).

Sequence Creation: The create_sequences function prepares the sequences with the correct number of features, avoiding the dimension mismatch error.

Saving Predictions: The predictions, along with the actual values and normalized predictions, are saved to a CSV file for further analysis.

This should resolve the dimension mismatch error you encountered. If you have a different feature that needs to be dropped, just replace 'normalized_z_score' with the correct column name. Let me know if you run into any more issues!

Certainly! Below is the full code that combines the LSTM model's predictions and the normalized z-scores into a single CSV file. python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate and Normalize Z-Scores
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler and normalize z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert only the normalized z-scores into the DataFrame
    df.insert(4, "normalized_z_score", normalized_z_scores)

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

# Example usage to preprocess the data and add z-scores
z_score_data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
addZscore(z_score_data_path)

# Step 2: Load the LSTM Model and Make Predictions
# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data with normalized z-scores
data = pd.read_csv(z_score_data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time' and one additional column to match the model's expected input shape)
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time', 'normalized_z_score'])  # Drop 'normalized_z_score'

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

sequence_length = 10
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Normalize the predictions
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(y_full_pred)

# Combine actual values, predictions, and normalized z-scores into a DataFrame
results_df = pd.DataFrame({
    'Actual_Usage_Amount': y,
    'Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred_normalized.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Z_Score': data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:].values  # Aligning the z-scores with the prediction indices
})

# Save the results to a CSV file
output_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\predictions_with_z_scores.csv"
results_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)
print(f"Predictions and Z-Scores saved to {output_path}")

# Optional: plot the actual vs predicted values
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred, color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred_normalized, color='orange', label='Normalized Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:], color='green', label='Normalized Z-Score')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted (Full Dataset) with Z-Scores')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Usage Amount')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Explanation:
Z-Score Calculation and Normalization: The addZscore function calculates z-scores for usage_amount, normalizes them, and adds them to the DataFrame.
LSTM Model Prediction: The LSTM model is loaded and used to make predictions on the prepared data.
Normalization of Predictions: Predictions are normalized using MinMaxScaler.
Combining Data: A DataFrame is created combining the actual usage amounts, LSTM model predictions, normalized predictions, and normalized z-scores.
Saving Results: The combined data is saved to a CSV file.
Visualization: The code includes an optional plot to visualize the actual usage amounts, predicted amounts, and z-scores.
Output:
The CSV file containing the actual usage amounts, LSTM predictions, normalized predictions, and normalized z-scores is saved to the specified path.
A plot is generated to visualize the data and predictions.
This should provide a comprehensive dataset that includes both your model's predictions and the z-scores, all normalized and ready for analysis.

"import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate and Normalize Z-Scores
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)

    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert only the normalized z-scores into the DataFrame
    df.insert(4, "normalized_z_score", normalized_z_scores)

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

ChatGPT said:
ChatGPT
The error you encountered is due to trying to insert the normalized_z_score column into the DataFrame when it already exists. This happens because the addZscore function is being called on a dataset that already contains the normalized_z_score column.

To fix this issue, you should check whether the normalized_z_score column already exists in the DataFrame before trying to insert it. If it exists, you can either skip the insertion or update the column.

Here's the corrected code:

Corrected Code:
python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate and Normalize Z-Scores
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler and normalize z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert or update the normalized z-scores in the DataFrame
    if 'normalized_z_score' in df.columns:
        df['normalized_z_score'] = normalized_z_scores
    else:
        df.insert(4, "normalized_z_score", normalized_z_scores)

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

# Example usage to preprocess the data and add z-scores
z_score_data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
addZscore(z_score_data_path)

# Step 2: Load the LSTM Model and Make Predictions
# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data with normalized z-scores
data = pd.read_csv(z_score_data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time' and one additional column to match the model's expected input shape)
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time', 'normalized_z_score'])  # Drop 'normalized_z_score'

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

sequence_length = 10
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Normalize the predictions
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(y_full_pred)

# Combine actual values, predictions, and normalized z-scores into a DataFrame
results_df = pd.DataFrame({
    'Actual_Usage_Amount': y,
    'Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred_normalized.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Z_Score': data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:].values  # Aligning the z-scores with the prediction indices
})

# Save the results to a CSV file
output_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\predictions_with_z_scores.csv"
results_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)
print(f"Predictions and Z-Scores saved to {output_path}")

# Optional: plot the actual vs predicted values
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred, color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred_normalized, color='orange', label='Normalized Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:], color='green', label='Normalized Z-Score')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted (Full Dataset) with Z-Scores')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Usage Amount')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Explanation:
Column Check Before Insertion: The addZscore function now checks if the normalized_z_score column already exists in the DataFrame. If it does, the column is updated with the new normalized z-scores. If it doesn't, the column is added.
CSV File Update: The normalized z-scores and model predictions are saved in a new CSV file along with the actual usage amounts.
This change should resolve the error and allow the code to run without issues. The output CSV will contain the combined results as expected.

"import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate and Normalize Z-Scores
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler and normalize z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert or update the normalized z-scores in the DataFrame
    if 'normalized_z_score' in df.columns:
        df['normalized_z_score'] = normalized_z_scores
    else:
        df.insert(4, "normalized_z_score", normalized_z_scores)

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

# Example usage to preprocess the data and add z-scores
z_score_data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
addZscore(z_score_data_path)

# Step 2: Load the LSTM Model and Make Predictions
# Load the saved LSTM model

model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data with normalized z-scores
data = pd.read_csv(z_score_data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time' and one additional column to match the model's expected input shape)
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time', 'normalized_z_score'])  # Drop 'normalized_z_score'

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

sequence_length = 10
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Normalize the predictions

# Combine actual values, predictions, and normalized z-scores into a DataFrame
results_df = pd.DataFrame({
    'Actual_Usage_Amount': y,
    'Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred_normalized.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Z_Score': data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:].values  # Aligning the z-scores with the prediction indices
})

# Save the results to a CSV file
output_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\predictions_with_z_scores.csv"
results_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)
print(f"Predictions and Z-Scores saved to {output_path}")

# Optional: plot the actual vs predicted values
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred, color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred_normalized, color='orange', label='Normalized Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:], color='green', label='Normalized Z-Score')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted (Full Dataset) with Z-Scores')

Updated Code:
python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate and Normalize Z-Scores
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler and normalize z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert or update the normalized z-scores in the DataFrame
    if 'normalized_z_score' in df.columns:
        df['normalized_z_score'] = normalized_z_scores
    else:
        df.insert(4, "normalized_z_score", normalized_z_scores)

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

# Example usage to preprocess the data and add z-scores
z_score_data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
addZscore(z_score_data_path)

# Step 2: Load the LSTM Model and Make Predictions
# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data with normalized z-scores
data = pd.read_csv(z_score_data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time' and one additional column to match the model's expected input shape)
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time', 'normalized_z_score'])  # Drop 'normalized_z_score'

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

sequence_length = 10
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Normalize the predictions
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(y_full_pred)

# Combine actual values, predictions, and normalized z-scores into a DataFrame
results_df = pd.DataFrame({
    'Actual_Usage_Amount': y,
    'Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred_normalized.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Z_Score': data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:].values  # Aligning the z-scores with the prediction indices
})

# Step 3: Multiply the Z-Scores with the Predictions and Normalize the Result
combined_scores = results_df['Normalized_Z_Score'] * results_df['Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount']

# Normalize the combined scores
combined_scores_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(combined_scores.values.reshape(-1, 1))

# Add the combined normalized scores to the DataFrame
results_df['Combined_Normalized_Score'] = combined_scores_normalized

# Save the results to a CSV file
output_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\predictions_with_combined_scores.csv"
results_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)
print(f"Predictions, Z-Scores, and Combined Scores saved to {output_path}")

# Optional: plot the actual vs predicted values
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred, color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(y_full_pred_normalized, color='orange', label='Normalized Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:], color='green', label='Normalized Z-Score')
plt.plot(combined_scores_normalized, color='purple', label='Combined Normalized Score')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted (Full Dataset) with Z-Scores and Combined Scores')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Usage Amount')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Explanation:
Multiplication of Z-Scores and Predictions: The code multiplies the normalized z-scores with the normalized predictions to create a new combined score.
Normalization of Combined Scores: The combined scores are normalized using MinMaxScaler.
Saving Combined Scores: The combined normalized scores are added to the results_df DataFrame and saved to a CSV file.
Plotting: The plot now includes the combined normalized scores along with the actual usage amounts, predicted amounts, and z-scores.
Output:
The resulting CSV file will contain the actual usage amounts, normalized predictions, normalized z-scores, and the combined normalized scores.
The plot will visualize all the relevant metrics, including the combined normalized score.
This approach gives you a comprehensive analysis of how the z-scores and predictions interact, with the combined scores providing an additional layer of insight.

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate and Normalize Z-Scores
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler and normalize z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert or update the normalized z-scores in the DataFrame
    if 'normalized_z_score' in df.columns:
        df['normalized_z_score'] = normalized_z_scores
    else:
        df.insert(4, "normalized_z_score", normalized_z_scores)

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

# Example usage to preprocess the data and add z-scores
z_score_data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
addZscore(z_score_data_path)

# Step 2: Load the LSTM Model and Make Predictions
# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data with normalized z-scores
data = pd.read_csv(z_score_data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time' and one additional column to match the model's expected input shape)
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time', 'normalized_z_score'])  # Drop 'normalized_z_score'

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

sequence_length = 10
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Normalize the predictions
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(y_full_pred)

# Combine actual values, predictions, and normalized z-scores into a DataFrame
results_df = pd.DataFrame({
    'Actual_Usage_Amount': y,
    'Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred_normalized.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Z_Score': data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:].values  # Aligning the z-scores with the prediction indices
})

# Step 3: Multiply the Z-Scores with the Predictions
combined_scores = results_df['Normalized_Z_Score'] * results_df['Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount']

# Add the combined scores to the DataFrame without normalizing this time
results_df['Combined_Score'] = combined_scores

# Save the results to a new CSV file
output_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\original_and_combined_scores.csv"
results_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)
print(f"Original values and Combined Scores saved to {output_path}")

# Optional: plot the actual vs predicted values
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(results_df['Actual_Usage_Amount'], color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(results_df['Predicted_Usage_Amount'], color='red', label='Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(results_df['Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount'], color='orange', label='Normalized Predicted Usage Amount')
plt.plot(results_df['Normalized_Z_Score'], color='green', label='Normalized Z-Score')
plt.plot(results_df['Combined_Score'], color='purple', label='Combined Score')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted with Z-Scores and Combined Scores')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Value')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Explanation:
Multiplication of Z-Scores and Predictions: The code multiplies the normalized z-scores with the normalized predictions to create a new combined score.
No Additional Normalization: The combined scores are added to the DataFrame without further normalization, keeping the original multiplied values.
Saving Original and Combined Values: A new CSV file is created that contains the original values (actual usage amounts, predicted amounts) and the newly computed combined scores.
Plotting: The plot shows the actual usage amounts, predicted values, normalized predictions, z-scores, and the combined scores.
Output:
CSV File: The output CSV file will include the original actual and predicted values, along with the combined scores.
Plot: The plot will visualize all the metrics, including the combined scores.
This approach ensures that you have both the original and the new computed values in a single dataset, providing a comprehensive view of your results.

To add the anomaly detection based on the combined score, you can introduce a new column in the DataFrame that marks entries where the combined score exceeds the threshold of 0.3 as anomalies. This will allow you to easily identify potential anomalies in the data.

Here’s the updated code with the anomaly detection added:

Updated Code:
python

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate and Normalize Z-Scores
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler and normalize z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert or update the normalized z-scores in the DataFrame
    if 'normalized_z_score' in df.columns:
        df['normalized_z_score'] = normalized_z_scores
    else:
        df.insert(4, "normalized_z_score", normalized_z_scores)

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

# Example usage to preprocess the data and add z-scores
z_score_data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
addZscore(z_score_data_path)

# Step 2: Load the LSTM Model and Make Predictions
# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data with normalized z-scores
data = pd.read_csv(z_score_data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time' and one additional column to match the model's expected input shape)
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time', 'normalized_z_score'])  # Drop 'normalized_z_score'

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

sequence_length = 10
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Normalize the predictions
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(y_full_pred)

# Combine actual values, predictions, and normalized z-scores into a DataFrame
results_df = pd.DataFrame({
    'Actual_Usage_Amount': y,
    'Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred_normalized.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Z_Score': data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:].values  # Aligning the z-scores with the prediction indices
})

# Step 3: Multiply the Z-Scores with the Predictions
combined_scores = results_df['Normalized_Z_Score'] * results_df['Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount']

# Add the combined scores to the DataFrame without normalizing this time
results_df['Combined_Score'] = combined_scores

# Step 4: Detect anomalies based on the combined score threshold
anomaly_threshold = 0.3
results_df['Anomaly'] = results_df['Combined_Score'] > anomaly_threshold

# Save the results to a new CSV file
output_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\original_and_combined_scores_with_anomalies.csv"
results_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)
print(f"Original values, Combined Scores, and Anomalies saved to {output_path}")

# Optional: plot the actual vs predicted values and highlight anomalies
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(results_df['Actual_Usage_Amount'], color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(results_df['Combined_Score'], color='purple', label='Combined Score')
plt.scatter(results_df.index[results_df['Anomaly']], results_df['Combined_Score'][results_df['Anomaly']], 
            color='red', label='Anomaly', marker='x')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted with Z-Scores and Combined Scores')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Value')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Explanation:
Anomaly Detection: After computing the combined score, the code checks if the combined score exceeds the threshold of 0.3. If it does, the corresponding entry is marked as an anomaly.
Anomaly Column: A new column, Anomaly, is added to the DataFrame. It contains True if the combined score exceeds 0.3, indicating a potential anomaly, and False otherwise.
CSV Output: The updated DataFrame, including the anomaly detections, is saved to a new CSV file.
Plotting with Anomalies: The plot now includes the combined scores and highlights potential anomalies with red x markers.
Output:
The resulting CSV file contains the original values, combined scores, and an additional column indicating potential anomalies.
The plot visualizes the data and highlights where anomalies have been detected.
This setup provides a clear indication of potential anomalies in the dataset based on the combined score.

"import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate and Normalize Z-Scores
def addZscore(path):
    df = pd.read_csv(path)
    c = 10
    n = len(df) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = df.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Initialize the MinMaxScaler and normalize z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))

    # Insert or update the normalized z-scores in the DataFrame
    if 'normalized_z_score' in df.columns:
        df['normalized_z_score'] = normalized_z_scores
    else:
        df.insert(4, "normalized_z_score", normalized_z_scores)

    # Save the modified DataFrame back to the CSV file
    df.to_csv(path, index=False)

# Example usage to preprocess the data and add z-scores
z_score_data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
addZscore(z_score_data_path)

# Step 2: Load the LSTM Model and Make Predictions
# Load the saved LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data with normalized z-scores
data = pd.read_csv(z_score_data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time' and one additional column to match the model's expected input shape)
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time', 'normalized_z_score'])  # Drop 'normalized_z_score'

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

sequence_length = 10
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions on the entire dataset
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Normalize the predictions
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(y_full_pred)

# Combine actual values, predictions, and normalized z-scores into a DataFrame
results_df = pd.DataFrame({
    'Actual_Usage_Amount': y,
    'Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount': y_full_pred_normalized.flatten(),
    'Normalized_Z_Score': data['normalized_z_score'][sequence_length:].values  # Aligning the z-scores with the prediction indices
})

# Step 3: Multiply the Z-Scores with the Predictions
combined_scores = results_df['Normalized_Z_Score'] * results_df['Normalized_Predicted_Usage_Amount']

# Add the combined scores to the DataFrame without normalizing this time
results_df['Combined_Score'] = combined_scores

# Step 4: Detect anomalies based on the combined score threshold
anomaly_threshold = 0.3
results_df['Anomaly'] = results_df['Combined_Score'] > anomaly_threshold

# Save the results to a new CSV file
output_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\original_and_combined_scores_with_anomalies.csv"
results_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)
print(f"Original values, Combined Scores, and Anomalies saved to {output_path}")

# Optional: plot the actual vs predicted values and highlight anomalies
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(results_df['Actual_Usage_Amount'], color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(results_df['Combined_Score'], color='purple', label='Combined Score')

            color='red', label='Anomaly', marker='x')
plt.title('LSTM Model - Actual vs Predicted with Z-Scores and Combined Scores')

plt.ylabel('Value')

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate Z-Scores and Normalize Them
def calculate_z_scores(data):
    c = 10
    n = len(data) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = data.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Normalize the z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))
    
    return normalized_z_scores.flatten()

# Load the LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data
data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
data = pd.read_csv(data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Calculate z-scores and normalize them
normalized_z_scores = calculate_z_scores(data)

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time' and 'normalized_z_score')
sequence_data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time'])

def create_sequences(data, seq_length):
    xs, ys = [], []
    for i in range(len(data) - seq_length):
        x = data.iloc[i:i+seq_length].values
        y = data.iloc[i+seq_length]['usage_amount']
        xs.append(x)
        ys.append(y)
    return np.array(xs), np.array(ys)

sequence_length = 10
X, y = create_sequences(sequence_data, sequence_length)
print(f"Sequences created. X shape: {X.shape}, y shape: {y.shape}")

# Make predictions
y_full_pred = model.predict(X)
print(f"Predictions on entire dataset completed. y_full_pred shape: {y_full_pred.shape}")

# Normalize the predictions
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(y_full_pred)

# Calculate the combined score
combined_scores = normalized_z_scores[sequence_length:] * y_full_pred_normalized.flatten()

# Plot the actual vs combined scores
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(combined_scores, color='purple', label='Combined Score')
plt.title('Actual Usage Amount vs Combined Score')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Value')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Explanation:
Calculate Z-Scores: The calculate_z_scores function calculates the z-scores for the usage_amount and normalizes them.
Model Predictions: The code makes predictions using the LSTM model and normalizes those predictions.
Combined Scores: The combined scores are calculated by multiplying the normalized z-scores with the normalized predicted values.
Plotting: The combined scores are plotted alongside the actual usage amounts.
Output:
Graph: The graph displays the actual usage amounts and the combined scores, allowing you to visually compare them.
This version of the code focuses solely on the key computational steps and visualization, removing any unnecessary complexity.

ChatGPT said:
ChatGPT
To modify the code so that it uses a moving time frame instead of fixed sequences, you'll need to adjust the way the data is processed and predicted. In this case, you can slide a moving window over the dataset to create inputs for the model. This method provides more flexibility by predicting values continuously as the window moves through the data.

Here’s the updated code:

Updated Code with Moving Time Frame:
python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate Z-Scores and Normalize Them
def calculate_z_scores(data):
    c = 10
    n = len(data) / c
    fin = []
    
    for i in range(1, c + 1):
        pre = int(n * (i - 1))
        post = int(n * i)
        temp = data.iloc[pre:post]
        z = np.array(temp["usage_amount"])
        zstat = list(stats.zscore(z))
        fin.extend(zstat)
    
    # Normalize the z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(fin).reshape(-1, 1))
    
    return normalized_z_scores.flatten()

# Load the LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the preprocessed data
data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\preprocessed_data.csv"
data = pd.read_csv(data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Calculate z-scores and normalize them
normalized_z_scores = calculate_z_scores(data)

# Prepare the data (excluding 'usage_end_time')
data = data.drop(columns=['usage_end_time'])

# Moving window parameters
window_size = 10
step_size = 1

# Initialize lists to store results
y_full_pred = []
y_actual = []

# Sliding window over the data
for i in range(0, len(data) - window_size, step_size):
    window_data = data.iloc[i:i+window_size].values
    y_actual.append(data.iloc[i + window_size]['usage_amount'])
    
    # Reshape the window data for prediction
    window_data = window_data.reshape(1, window_size, -1)
    
    # Predict the next value
    pred = model.predict(window_data)
    y_full_pred.append(pred[0, 0])

# Normalize the predictions
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(y_full_pred).reshape(-1, 1)).flatten()

# Calculate the combined score
combined_scores = normalized_z_scores[window_size:] * y_full_pred_normalized

# Plot the actual vs combined scores
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y_actual, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(combined_scores, color='purple', label='Combined Score')
plt.title('Actual Usage Amount vs Combined Score with Moving Time Frame')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Value')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Explanation:
Moving Window: The code uses a moving window to slide over the dataset, predicting the next value at each step. The window size determines how many data points are used to make each prediction, while the step size controls the movement of the window.
Continuous Predictions: The model makes predictions continuously as the window slides over the dataset, which is then compared to the actual data.
Normalization: The predictions are normalized before being multiplied with the z-scores to create the combined score.
Plotting: The combined score and the actual usage amount are plotted to visualize the comparison.
Output:
Graph: The graph displays the actual usage amounts and the combined scores, allowing you to compare them directly.
This approach allows you to predict usage amounts continuously over time using a moving window, making the predictions more flexible and applicable to real-time scenarios.
