"import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler, OneHotEncoder
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate Z-Scores and Normalize Them
def calculate_z_scores(usage_amount):
    print("Calculating z-scores for 'usage_amount' column...")
    # Calculate z-scores for the 'usage_amount' column
    z_scores = stats.zscore(usage_amount)
    print(f"Z-scores calculated: mean={np.mean(z_scores):.4f}, std={np.std(z_scores):.4f}")
    
    # Normalize the z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(z_scores.reshape(-1, 1))
    print("Z-scores normalized.")
    
    return normalized_z_scores.flatten()

# Load the LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
print(f"Loading LSTM model from {model_path}...")
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the specific dataset
data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\split_data\Cloud Storage TEST DO NOT USE.csv"
print(f"Loading data from {data_path}...")
data = pd.read_csv(data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Convert 'usage_end_time' to datetime
print("Converting 'usage_end_time' to datetime...")
data['usage_end_time'] = pd.to_datetime(data['usage_end_time'])

# Aggregate data by hourly usage
print("Aggregating data by hourly intervals...")
hourly_data = data.resample('H', on='usage_end_time').agg({
    'usage_amount': 'sum',
    'cost': 'sum',  # You may include this if needed
    'service_type': lambda x: x.mode()[0]  # Keep the most frequent service_type
}).reset_index()

print(f"Hourly aggregated data shape: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Preserve 'usage_amount' for later use
usage_amount = hourly_data['usage_amount'].values
print(f"Preserved 'usage_amount' with {len(usage_amount)} entries.")

# One-Hot Encode categorical variables
print("One-Hot Encoding 'service_type' column...")
encoder = OneHotEncoder(sparse_output=False)
encoded_features = encoder.fit_transform(hourly_data[['service_type']])
print(f"One-Hot Encoding completed. Encoded features shape: {encoded_features.shape}")

# Create a DataFrame with the encoded features
encoded_df = pd.DataFrame(encoded_features, columns=encoder.get_feature_names_out(['service_type']))

# Concatenate the encoded features with the original DataFrame
print("Concatenating encoded features with original data...")
hourly_data = pd.concat([hourly_data.drop(columns=['service_type', 'usage_end_time']), encoded_df], axis=1)
print(f"Data shape after concatenation: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Ensure the number of features matches the model's input
expected_features = model.input_shape[-1]  # Number of features the model expects
current_features = hourly_data.shape[1]
print(f"Expected features: {expected_features}, Current features: {current_features}")

# Select features that align with the model's training data
if current_features != expected_features:
    if current_features > expected_features:
        print(f"Warning: Model expects {expected_features} features, but the data has {current_features}. Truncating to match the expected number of features.")
        hourly_data = hourly_data.iloc[:, :expected_features]  # Select the first 'expected_features' columns
    else:
        print(f"Padding data with {expected_features - current_features} zeros to match the expected features.")
        # Pad the data with zeros if there are fewer features
        padding = np.zeros((hourly_data.shape[0], expected_features - current_features))
        hourly_data = np.hstack((hourly_data.values, padding))
        hourly_data = pd.DataFrame(hourly_data)  # Convert back to DataFrame
        print(f"Data shape after padding: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Calculate z-scores and normalize them
normalized_z_scores = calculate_z_scores(usage_amount)

# Moving window parameters (can be adjusted for optimization)
window_size = 50  # Typical values might range from 10 to 50 depending on the data
step_size = 1

print(f"Starting sliding window predictions with window size: {window_size} and step size: {step_size}...")

# Initialize lists to store results
y_full_pred = []
y_actual = []

# Sliding window over the data
for i in range(0, len(hourly_data) - window_size, step_size):
    if i % 10 == 0:  # Reduced frequency for large datasets
        print(f"Processing window {i} of {len(hourly_data) - window_size}...")
    
    window_data = hourly_data.iloc[i:i+window_size].values.astype(np.float32)  # Ensure the data is in float32
    y_actual.append(usage_amount[i + window_size])  # Use preserved 'usage_amount' values
    
    # Reshape the window data for prediction
    window_data = window_data.reshape(1, window_size, -1)
    
    # Predict the next value
    pred = model.predict(window_data)
    y_full_pred.append(pred[0, 0])

# Normalize the predictions
print("Normalizing predictions...")
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(y_full_pred).reshape(-1, 1)).flatten()

# Calculate the combined score
print("Calculating combined scores...")
combined_scores = normalized_z_scores[window_size:] * y_full_pred_normalized

# Plot the actual vs combined scores
print("Plotting the results...")
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y_actual, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(combined_scores, color='purple', label='Combined Score')
plt.title('Actual Usage Amount vs Combined Score with Moving Time Frame')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Value')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
"

ChatGPT
The error you encountered suggests that there was an issue when attempting to aggregate the service_type column using the mode function. Specifically, it seems like there was a problem with finding the mode or accessing the value in the grouped data, potentially because the group might be empty or the mode() function didn't return a result in some cases.

To address this, we'll modify the code to handle cases where the mode might not be found by providing a fallback. We'll also add additional debugging statements to help track the data at each step.

Here's the updated code:

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler, OneHotEncoder
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate Z-Scores and Normalize Them
def calculate_z_scores(usage_amount):
    print("Calculating z-scores for 'usage_amount' column...")
    # Calculate z-scores for the 'usage_amount' column
    z_scores = stats.zscore(usage_amount)
    print(f"Z-scores calculated: mean={np.mean(z_scores):.4f}, std={np.std(z_scores):.4f}")
    
    # Normalize the z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(z_scores.reshape(-1, 1))
    print("Z-scores normalized.")
    
    return normalized_z_scores.flatten()

# Load the LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
print(f"Loading LSTM model from {model_path}...")
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the specific dataset
data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\split_data\Cloud Storage TEST DO NOT USE.csv"
print(f"Loading data from {data_path}...")
data = pd.read_csv(data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Convert 'usage_end_time' to datetime
print("Converting 'usage_end_time' to datetime...")
data['usage_end_time'] = pd.to_datetime(data['usage_end_time'])

# Aggregate data by hourly usage
print("Aggregating data by hourly intervals...")
def get_most_frequent(x):
    if len(x) == 0:
        return 'Unknown'
    return x.mode()[0] if not x.mode().empty else 'Unknown'

hourly_data = data.resample('H', on='usage_end_time').agg({
    'usage_amount': 'sum',
    'cost': 'sum',  # You may include this if needed
    'service_type': get_most_frequent  # Keep the most frequent service_type with fallback
}).reset_index()

print(f"Hourly aggregated data shape: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Preserve 'usage_amount' for later use
usage_amount = hourly_data['usage_amount'].values
print(f"Preserved 'usage_amount' with {len(usage_amount)} entries.")

# One-Hot Encode categorical variables
print("One-Hot Encoding 'service_type' column...")
encoder = OneHotEncoder(sparse_output=False)
encoded_features = encoder.fit_transform(hourly_data[['service_type']])
print(f"One-Hot Encoding completed. Encoded features shape: {encoded_features.shape}")

# Create a DataFrame with the encoded features
encoded_df = pd.DataFrame(encoded_features, columns=encoder.get_feature_names_out(['service_type']))

# Concatenate the encoded features with the original DataFrame
print("Concatenating encoded features with original data...")
hourly_data = pd.concat([hourly_data.drop(columns=['service_type', 'usage_end_time']), encoded_df], axis=1)
print(f"Data shape after concatenation: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Ensure the number of features matches the model's input
expected_features = model.input_shape[-1]  # Number of features the model expects
current_features = hourly_data.shape[1]
print(f"Expected features: {expected_features}, Current features: {current_features}")

# Select features that align with the model's training data
if current_features != expected_features:
    if current_features > expected_features:
        print(f"Warning: Model expects {expected_features} features, but the data has {current_features}. Truncating to match the expected number of features.")
        hourly_data = hourly_data.iloc[:, :expected_features]  # Select the first 'expected_features' columns
    else:
        print(f"Padding data with {expected_features - current_features} zeros to match the expected features.")
        # Pad the data with zeros if there are fewer features
        padding = np.zeros((hourly_data.shape[0], expected_features - current_features))
        hourly_data = np.hstack((hourly_data.values, padding))
        hourly_data = pd.DataFrame(hourly_data)  # Convert back to DataFrame
        print(f"Data shape after padding: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Calculate z-scores and normalize them
normalized_z_scores = calculate_z_scores(usage_amount)

# Moving window parameters (can be adjusted for optimization)
window_size = 50  # Typical values might range from 10 to 50 depending on the data
step_size = 1

print(f"Starting sliding window predictions with window size: {window_size} and step size: {step_size}...")

# Initialize lists to store results
y_full_pred = []
y_actual = []

# Sliding window over the data
for i in range(0, len(hourly_data) - window_size, step_size):
    if i % 10 == 0:  # Reduced frequency for large datasets
        print(f"Processing window {i} of {len(hourly_data) - window_size}...")
    
    window_data = hourly_data.iloc[i:i+window_size].values.astype(np.float32)  # Ensure the data is in float32
    y_actual.append(usage_amount[i + window_size])  # Use preserved 'usage_amount' values
    
    # Reshape the window data for prediction
    window_data = window_data.reshape(1, window_size, -1)
    
    # Predict the next value
    pred = model.predict(window_data)
    y_full_pred.append(pred[0, 0])

# Normalize the predictions
print("Normalizing predictions...")
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(y_full_pred).reshape(-1, 1)).flatten()

# Calculate the combined score
print("Calculating combined scores...")
combined_scores = normalized_z_scores[window_size:] * y_full_pred_normalized

# Plot the actual vs combined scores
print("Plotting the results...")
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y_actual, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(combined_scores, color='purple', label='Combined Score')
plt.title('Actual Usage Amount vs Combined Score with Moving Time Frame')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Value')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Key Changes:
Error Handling in Mode Calculation: The function get_most_frequent(x) has been added to safely handle cases where the mode might not be found or when the group is empty. It provides a fallback value ('Unknown') in such cases.
Debugging and Status Prints: Additional print statements have been added to give detailed feedback about the process and to track where the script might be failing.
This should help resolve the issues you encountered and make the code more robust against edge cases in the data.

ChatGPT said:
ChatGPT
The code appears to aggregate the data into hourly intervals, sum the usage_amount and cost, and handle the categorical service_type column by taking the mode. However, let’s ensure that all steps align properly with the intended hourly-based analysis:

Key Checks:
Aggregation to Hours:

The data.resample('H', on='usage_end_time') line correctly resamples the data to hourly intervals.
The aggregation functions applied (sum for usage_amount and cost, and mode for service_type) are appropriate for this purpose.
Preservation of usage_amount:

After aggregation, usage_amount values are correctly preserved for further analysis.
Categorical Encoding:

One-Hot Encoding is applied to service_type after the hourly aggregation, which is appropriate.
Feature Alignment:

The code checks and adjusts the number of features to match what the LSTM model expects, padding with zeros if necessary or truncating excess features.
Sliding Window Processing:

The sliding window approach works on the resampled and aggregated data, which should ensure that the analysis is based on hourly intervals.
Debugging and Status Prints:

There are comprehensive debug prints throughout the code to track the process at each step.
Conclusion:
Yes, the code is set up to properly convert the data into hourly intervals, and it then processes this hourly data through the LSTM model using the sliding window approach.

Potential Improvements:
Edge Case Handling: If the usage_amount or service_type columns contain NaN values after resampling, you might want to handle those explicitly.
Efficiency: Depending on the dataset size, consider whether the padding/truncation approach in feature alignment is the most efficient for your use case.
Next Steps:
Run the code to verify its correctness with your dataset.
Monitor the output for any unexpected behavior, especially in the aggregation and encoding steps.

"import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler, OneHotEncoder
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate Z-Scores and Normalize Them
def calculate_z_scores(usage_amount):
    print("Calculating z-scores for 'usage_amount' column...")
    # Calculate z-scores for the 'usage_amount' column
    z_scores = stats.zscore(usage_amount)
    print(f"Z-scores calculated: mean={np.mean(z_scores):.4f}, std={np.std(z_scores):.4f}")
    
    # Normalize the z-scores
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(z_scores.reshape(-1, 1))
    print("Z-scores normalized.")
    
    return normalized_z_scores.flatten()

# Load the LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
print(f"Loading LSTM model from {model_path}...")
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the specific dataset
data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\split_data\Cloud Storage TEST DO NOT USE.csv"
print(f"Loading data from {data_path}...")
data = pd.read_csv(data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Convert 'usage_end_time' to datetime
print("Converting 'usage_end_time' to datetime...")
data['usage_end_time'] = pd.to_datetime(data['usage_end_time'])

# Aggregate data by hourly usage
print("Aggregating data by hourly intervals...")
def get_most_frequent(x):
    if len(x) == 0:
        return 'Unknown'
    return x.mode()[0] if not x.mode().empty else 'Unknown'

hourly_data = data.resample('H', on='usage_end_time').agg({
    'usage_amount': 'sum',
    'cost': 'sum',  # You may include this if needed
    'service_type': get_most_frequent  # Keep the most frequent service_type with fallback
}).reset_index()

print(f"Hourly aggregated data shape: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Preserve 'usage_amount' for later use
usage_amount = hourly_data['usage_amount'].values
print(f"Preserved 'usage_amount' with {len(usage_amount)} entries.")

# One-Hot Encode categorical variables
print("One-Hot Encoding 'service_type' column...")
encoder = OneHotEncoder(sparse_output=False)
encoded_features = encoder.fit_transform(hourly_data[['service_type']])
print(f"One-Hot Encoding completed. Encoded features shape: {encoded_features.shape}")

# Create a DataFrame with the encoded features
encoded_df = pd.DataFrame(encoded_features, columns=encoder.get_feature_names_out(['service_type']))

# Concatenate the encoded features with the original DataFrame
print("Concatenating encoded features with original data...")
hourly_data = pd.concat([hourly_data.drop(columns=['service_type', 'usage_end_time']), encoded_df], axis=1)
print(f"Data shape after concatenation: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Ensure the number of features matches the model's input
expected_features = model.input_shape[-1]  # Number of features the model expects
current_features = hourly_data.shape[1]
print(f"Expected features: {expected_features}, Current features: {current_features}")

# Select features that align with the model's training data
if current_features != expected_features:
    if current_features > expected_features:
        print(f"Warning: Model expects {expected_features} features, but the data has {current_features}. Truncating to match the expected number of features.")
        hourly_data = hourly_data.iloc[:, :expected_features]  # Select the first 'expected_features' columns
    else:
        print(f"Padding data with {expected_features - current_features} zeros to match the expected features.")
        # Pad the data with zeros if there are fewer features
        padding = np.zeros((hourly_data.shape[0], expected_features - current_features))
        hourly_data = np.hstack((hourly_data.values, padding))
        hourly_data = pd.DataFrame(hourly_data)  # Convert back to DataFrame
        print(f"Data shape after padding: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Calculate z-scores and normalize them
normalized_z_scores = calculate_z_scores(usage_amount)

# Moving window parameters (can be adjusted for optimization)
window_size = 50  # Typical values might range from 10 to 50 depending on the data
step_size = 1

print(f"Starting sliding window predictions with window size: {window_size} and step size: {step_size}...")

# Initialize lists to store results
y_full_pred = []
y_actual = []

# Sliding window over the data
for i in range(0, len(hourly_data) - window_size, step_size):
    if i % 10 == 0:  # Reduced frequency for large datasets
        print(f"Processing window {i} of {len(hourly_data) - window_size}...")
    
    window_data = hourly_data.iloc[i:i+window_size].values.astype(np.float32)  # Ensure the data is in float32
    y_actual.append(usage_amount[i + window_size])  # Use preserved 'usage_amount' values
    
    # Reshape the window data for prediction
    window_data = window_data.reshape(1, window_size, -1)
    
    # Predict the next value
    pred = model.predict(window_data)
    y_full_pred.append(pred[0, 0])

# Normalize the predictions
print("Normalizing predictions...")
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(y_full_pred).reshape(-1, 1)).flatten()

# Calculate the combined score
print("Calculating combined scores...")
combined_scores = normalized_z_scores[window_size:] * y_full_pred_normalized

# Plot the actual vs combined scores
print("Plotting the results...")
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y_actual, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(combined_scores, color='purple', label='Combined Score')
plt.title('Actual Usage Amount vs Combined Score with Moving Time Frame')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Value')
plt.legend()
plt.show()

ChatGPT said:
ChatGPT
The issue of data "holes" (where the usage_amount might suddenly drop to zero and then rise again) can arise from the resampling process, particularly if there are time periods in the original dataset with no records. Resampling with pandas' resample function can introduce these gaps, especially if there are missing timestamps in the original data.

Here’s how we can address and check for these issues:
Ensure Continuous Timestamps:

Before resampling, ensure that the original dataset is indexed by usage_end_time and any missing timestamps are filled appropriately.
Fill Missing Data After Resampling:

After resampling, if there are periods where no data was recorded, these periods will appear as zeros after summing. These zeros might not represent the true state of the system. Consider using methods like forward-filling (ffill), backward-filling (bfill), or interpolating to smooth out these gaps.
Check for Data Holes:

After resampling, visually inspect or print out sections of the data to check for unexpected drops to zero.
Here’s how to incorporate these checks and corrections into your code:

python
Copy code
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler, OneHotEncoder
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate Z-Scores and Normalize Them
def calculate_z_scores(usage_amount):
    print("Calculating z-scores for 'usage_amount' column...")
    z_scores = stats.zscore(usage_amount)
    print(f"Z-scores calculated: mean={np.mean(z_scores):.4f}, std={np.std(z_scores):.4f}")
    
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(z_scores.reshape(-1, 1))
    print("Z-scores normalized.")
    
    return normalized_z_scores.flatten()

# Load the LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
print(f"Loading LSTM model from {model_path}...")
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the specific dataset
data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\split_data\Cloud Storage TEST DO NOT USE.csv"
print(f"Loading data from {data_path}...")
data = pd.read_csv(data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Convert 'usage_end_time' to datetime
print("Converting 'usage_end_time' to datetime...")
data['usage_end_time'] = pd.to_datetime(data['usage_end_time'])

# Reindex to ensure all timestamps are present
print("Reindexing data to ensure all hourly timestamps are present...")
data = data.set_index('usage_end_time')
all_hours = pd.date_range(start=data.index.min(), end=data.index.max(), freq='H')
data = data.reindex(all_hours, fill_value=0).reset_index().rename(columns={'index': 'usage_end_time'})

# Aggregate data by hourly usage
print("Aggregating data by hourly intervals...")
def get_most_frequent(x):
    if len(x) == 0:
        return 'Unknown'
    return x.mode()[0] if not x.mode().empty else 'Unknown'

hourly_data = data.resample('H', on='usage_end_time').agg({
    'usage_amount': 'sum',
    'cost': 'sum',
    'service_type': get_most_frequent
}).reset_index()

print(f"Hourly aggregated data shape: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Preserve 'usage_amount' for later use
usage_amount = hourly_data['usage_amount'].values
print(f"Preserved 'usage_amount' with {len(usage_amount)} entries.")

# Fill any remaining gaps with interpolation (optional)
print("Interpolating missing values in 'usage_amount'...")
hourly_data['usage_amount'] = hourly_data['usage_amount'].replace(0, np.nan).interpolate()

# One-Hot Encode categorical variables
print("One-Hot Encoding 'service_type' column...")
encoder = OneHotEncoder(sparse_output=False)
encoded_features = encoder.fit_transform(hourly_data[['service_type']])
print(f"One-Hot Encoding completed. Encoded features shape: {encoded_features.shape}")

# Create a DataFrame with the encoded features
encoded_df = pd.DataFrame(encoded_features, columns=encoder.get_feature_names_out(['service_type']))

# Concatenate the encoded features with the original DataFrame
print("Concatenating encoded features with original data...")
hourly_data = pd.concat([hourly_data.drop(columns=['service_type', 'usage_end_time']), encoded_df], axis=1)
print(f"Data shape after concatenation: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Ensure the number of features matches the model's input
expected_features = model.input_shape[-1]
current_features = hourly_data.shape[1]
print(f"Expected features: {expected_features}, Current features: {current_features}")

if current_features != expected_features:
    if current_features > expected_features:
        print(f"Warning: Model expects {expected_features} features, but the data has {current_features}. Truncating to match the expected number of features.")
        hourly_data = hourly_data.iloc[:, :expected_features]
    else:
        print(f"Padding data with {expected_features - current_features} zeros to match the expected features.")
        padding = np.zeros((hourly_data.shape[0], expected_features - current_features))
        hourly_data = np.hstack((hourly_data.values, padding))
        hourly_data = pd.DataFrame(hourly_data)
        print(f"Data shape after padding: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Calculate z-scores and normalize them
normalized_z_scores = calculate_z_scores(usage_amount)

# Moving window parameters
window_size = 50
step_size = 1

print(f"Starting sliding window predictions with window size: {window_size} and step size: {step_size}...")

# Initialize lists to store results
y_full_pred = []
y_actual = []

# Sliding window over the data
for i in range(0, len(hourly_data) - window_size, step_size):
    if i % 10 == 0:
        print(f"Processing window {i} of {len(hourly_data) - window_size}...")
    
    window_data = hourly_data.iloc[i:i+window_size].values.astype(np.float32)
    y_actual.append(usage_amount[i + window_size])
    
    window_data = window_data.reshape(1, window_size, -1)
    pred = model.predict(window_data)
    y_full_pred.append(pred[0, 0])

# Normalize the predictions
print("Normalizing predictions...")
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(y_full_pred).reshape(-1, 1)).flatten()

# Calculate the combined score
print("Calculating combined scores...")
combined_scores = normalized_z_scores[window_size:] * y_full_pred_normalized

# Plot the actual vs combined scores
print("Plotting the results...")
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y_actual, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(combined_scores, color='purple', label='Combined Score')
plt.title('Actual Usage Amount vs Combined Score with Moving Time Frame')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Value')
plt.legend()
plt.show()
Key Changes:
Reindexing: Added reindex to ensure that the dataset contains all hourly timestamps, filling any missing timestamps with zero values before aggregation.
Interpolation: After aggregation, I included a step to interpolate missing values to smooth out the data. This prevents sudden drops to zero in the usage_amount that are not due to actual lack of usage.
This should help in reducing the appearance of artificial "holes" in the data after resampling. Please test the modified code and verify that it corrects the issue.

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler, OneHotEncoder
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate Z-Scores and Normalize Them
def calculate_z_scores(usage_amount):
    print("Calculating z-scores for 'usage_amount' column...")
    z_scores = stats.zscore(usage_amount)
    print(f"Z-scores calculated: mean={np.mean(z_scores):.4f}, std={np.std(z_scores):.4f}")
    
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(z_scores.reshape(-1, 1))
    print("Z-scores normalized.")
    
    return normalized_z_scores.flatten()

# Load the LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
print(f"Loading LSTM model from {model_path}...")
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the specific dataset
data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\split_data\Cloud Storage TEST DO NOT USE.csv"
print(f"Loading data from {data_path}...")
data = pd.read_csv(data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Convert 'usage_end_time' to datetime
print("Converting 'usage_end_time' to datetime...")
data['usage_end_time'] = pd.to_datetime(data['usage_end_time'])

# Check for and handle duplicates
print("Checking for duplicates in 'usage_end_time'...")
if data.duplicated(subset='usage_end_time').any():
    print("Duplicates found. Aggregating duplicate entries...")
    data = data.groupby('usage_end_time').agg({
        'usage_amount': 'sum',
        'cost': 'sum',
        'service_type': lambda x: x.mode()[0] if not x.mode().empty else 'Unknown'
    }).reset_index()

# Reindex to ensure all timestamps are present
print("Reindexing data to ensure all hourly timestamps are present...")
data = data.set_index('usage_end_time')
all_hours = pd.date_range(start=data.index.min(), end=data.index.max(), freq='H')
data = data.reindex(all_hours, fill_value=0).reset_index().rename(columns={'index': 'usage_end_time'})

# Aggregate data by hourly usage (This step may be redundant depending on previous aggregation)
print("Aggregating data by hourly intervals...")
hourly_data = data.resample('H', on='usage_end_time').agg({
    'usage_amount': 'sum',
    'cost': 'sum',
    'service_type': lambda x: x.mode()[0] if not x.mode().empty else 'Unknown'
}).reset_index()

print(f"Hourly aggregated data shape: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Preserve 'usage_amount' for later use
usage_amount = hourly_data['usage_amount'].values
print(f"Preserved 'usage_amount' with {len(usage_amount)} entries.")

# One-Hot Encode categorical variables
print("One-Hot Encoding 'service_type' column...")
encoder = OneHotEncoder(sparse_output=False)
encoded_features = encoder.fit_transform(hourly_data[['service_type']])
print(f"One-Hot Encoding completed. Encoded features shape: {encoded_features.shape}")

# Create a DataFrame with the encoded features
encoded_df = pd.DataFrame(encoded_features, columns=encoder.get_feature_names_out(['service_type']))

# Concatenate the encoded features with the original DataFrame
print("Concatenating encoded features with original data...")
hourly_data = pd.concat([hourly_data.drop(columns=['service_type', 'usage_end_time']), encoded_df], axis=1)
print(f"Data shape after concatenation: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Ensure the number of features matches the model's input
expected_features = model.input_shape[-1]
current_features = hourly_data.shape[1]
print(f"Expected features: {expected_features}, Current features: {current_features}")

if current_features != expected_features:
    if current_features > expected_features:
        print(f"Warning: Model expects {expected_features} features, but the data has {current_features}. Truncating to match the expected number of features.")
        hourly_data = hourly_data.iloc[:, :expected_features]
    else:
        print(f"Padding data with {expected_features - current_features} zeros to match the expected features.")
        padding = np.zeros((hourly_data.shape[0], expected_features - current_features))
        hourly_data = np.hstack((hourly_data.values, padding))
        hourly_data = pd.DataFrame(hourly_data)
        print(f"Data shape after padding: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Calculate z-scores and normalize them
normalized_z_scores = calculate_z_scores(usage_amount)

# Moving window parameters
window_size = 50
step_size = 1

print(f"Starting sliding window predictions with window size: {window_size} and step size: {step_size}...")

# Initialize lists to store results
y_full_pred = []
y_actual = []

# Sliding window over the data
for i in range(0, len(hourly_data) - window_size, step_size):
    if i % 10 == 0:
        print(f"Processing window {i} of {len(hourly_data) - window_size}...")
    
    window_data = hourly_data.iloc[i:i+window_size].values.astype(np.float32)
    y_actual.append(usage_amount[i + window_size])
    
    window_data = window_data.reshape(1, window_size, -1)
    pred = model.predict(window_data)
    y_full_pred.append(pred[0, 0])

# Normalize the predictions
print("Normalizing predictions...")
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(y_full_pred).reshape(-1, 1)).flatten()

# Calculate the combined score
print("Calculating combined scores...")
combined_scores = normalized_z_scores[window_size:] * y_full_pred_normalized

# Plot the actual vs combined scores
print("Plotting the results...")
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y_actual, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(combined_scores, color='purple', label='Combined Score')
plt.title('Actual Usage Amount vs Combined Score with Moving Time Frame')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Value')
plt.legend()
plt.show()

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler, OneHotEncoder
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate Z-Scores and Normalize Them
def calculate_z_scores(usage_amount):
    print("Calculating z-scores for 'usage_amount' column...")
    z_scores = stats.zscore(usage_amount)
    print(f"Z-scores calculated: mean={np.mean(z_scores):.4f}, std={np.std(z_scores):.4f}")
    
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(z_scores.reshape(-1, 1))
    print("Z-scores normalized.")
    
    return normalized_z_scores.flatten()

# Load the LSTM model
model_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\LSTM\1.lstm_model.h5"
print(f"Loading LSTM model from {model_path}...")
model = load_model(model_path)
print("Model loaded successfully.")

# Load the specific dataset
data_path = r"C:\Users\<redacted-user>\Documents\Hackathon 2024\Hackathon2024\SRC\Data\split_data\Cloud Storage TEST DO NOT USE.csv"
print(f"Loading data from {data_path}...")
data = pd.read_csv(data_path)
print(f"Data loaded successfully with shape: {data.shape}")

# Convert 'usage_end_time' to datetime
print("Converting 'usage_end_time' to datetime...")
data['usage_end_time'] = pd.to_datetime(data['usage_end_time'])

# Check for and handle duplicates
print("Checking for duplicates in 'usage_end_time'...")
if data.duplicated(subset='usage_end_time').any():
    print("Duplicates found. Aggregating duplicate entries...")
    data = data.groupby('usage_end_time').agg({
        'usage_amount': 'sum',
        'cost': 'sum',
        'service_type': lambda x: x.mode()[0] if not x.mode().empty else 'Unknown'
    }).reset_index()

# Reindex to ensure all timestamps are present
print("Reindexing data to ensure all hourly timestamps are present...")
data = data.set_index('usage_end_time')
all_hours = pd.date_range(start=data.index.min(), end=data.index.max(), freq='H')
data = data.reindex(all_hours, fill_value=0).reset_index().rename(columns={'index': 'usage_end_time'})

# Aggregate data by hourly usage (This step may be redundant depending on previous aggregation)
print("Aggregating data by hourly intervals...")
hourly_data = data.resample('H', on='usage_end_time').agg({
    'usage_amount': 'sum',
    'cost': 'sum',
    'service_type': lambda x: x.mode()[0] if not x.mode().empty else 'Unknown'
}).reset_index()

print(f"Hourly aggregated data shape: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Convert 'service_type' to a string to ensure uniform data type
hourly_data['service_type'] = hourly_data['service_type'].astype(str)

# Preserve 'usage_amount' for later use
usage_amount = hourly_data['usage_amount'].values
print(f"Preserved 'usage_amount' with {len(usage_amount)} entries.")

# One-Hot Encode categorical variables
print("One-Hot Encoding 'service_type' column...")
encoder = OneHotEncoder(sparse_output=False)
encoded_features = encoder.fit_transform(hourly_data[['service_type']])
print(f"One-Hot Encoding completed. Encoded features shape: {encoded_features.shape}")

# Create a DataFrame with the encoded features
encoded_df = pd.DataFrame(encoded_features, columns=encoder.get_feature_names_out(['service_type']))

# Concatenate the encoded features with the original DataFrame
print("Concatenating encoded features with original data...")
hourly_data = pd.concat([hourly_data.drop(columns=['service_type', 'usage_end_time']), encoded_df], axis=1)
print(f"Data shape after concatenation: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Ensure the number of features matches the model's input
expected_features = model.input_shape[-1]
current_features = hourly_data.shape[1]
print(f"Expected features: {expected_features}, Current features: {current_features}")

if current_features != expected_features:
    if current_features > expected_features:
        print(f"Warning: Model expects {expected_features} features, but the data has {current_features}. Truncating to match the expected number of features.")
        hourly_data = hourly_data.iloc[:, :expected_features]
    else:
        print(f"Padding data with {expected_features - current_features} zeros to match the expected features.")
        padding = np.zeros((hourly_data.shape[0], expected_features - current_features))
        hourly_data = np.hstack((hourly_data.values, padding))
        hourly_data = pd.DataFrame(hourly_data)
        print(f"Data shape after padding: {hourly_data.shape}")

# Calculate z-scores and normalize them
normalized_z_scores = calculate_z_scores(usage_amount)

# Moving window parameters
window_size = 50
step_size = 1

print(f"Starting sliding window predictions with window size: {window_size} and step size: {step_size}...")

# Initialize lists to store results
y_full_pred = []
y_actual = []

# Sliding window over the data
for i in range(0, len(hourly_data) - window_size, step_size):
    if i % 10 == 0:
        print(f"Processing window {i} of {len(hourly_data) - window_size}...")
    
    window_data = hourly_data.iloc[i:i+window_size].values.astype(np.float32)
    y_actual.append(usage_amount[i + window_size])
    
    window_data = window_data.reshape(1, window_size, -1)
    pred = model.predict(window_data)
    y_full_pred.append(pred[0, 0])

# Normalize the predictions
print("Normalizing predictions...")
scaler = MinMaxScaler()
y_full_pred_normalized = scaler.fit_transform(np.array(y_full_pred).reshape(-1, 1)).flatten()

# Calculate the combined score
print("Calculating combined scores...")
combined_scores = normalized_z_scores[window_size:] * y_full_pred_normalized

# Plot the actual vs combined scores
print("Plotting the results...")
plt.figure(figsize=(12, 6))
plt.plot(y_actual, color='blue', label='Actual Usage Amount')
plt.plot(combined_scores, color='purple', label='Combined Score')
plt.title('Actual Usage Amount vs Combined Score with Moving Time Frame')
plt.xlabel('Time Step')
plt.ylabel('Value')
plt.legend()
plt.show()

Convert service_type to String: This ensures that all values in the service_type column are treated as strings before one-hot encoding. This should prevent the TypeError you encountered.
Try running the updated code, and this should resolve the issue.

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import scipy.stats as stats
from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler, OneHotEncoder
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Step 1: Calculate Z-Scores and Normalize Them
def calculate_z_scores(usage_amount):
    print("Calculating z-scores for 'usage_amount' column...")
    z_scores = stats.zscore(np.log1p(usage_amount))  # Apply log1p transformation to reduce large value effect
    print(f"Z-scores calculated: mean={np.mean(z_scores):.4f}, std={np.std(z_scores):.4f}")
    
    scaler = MinMaxScaler()
    normalized_z_scores = scaler.fit_transform(z_scores.reshape(-1, 1))
    print("Z-scores normalized.")
    
    return normalized_z_scores.flatten()

""" if value > self.threshold: print(f"Anomaly detected for value {value}") return 1 # Anomaly else: return 0 # Normal def update_model_attributes(self, value): """ Update the model attributes after processing a new data point. """ # Update threshold (example: adjust based on new value) self.threshold = np.mean(self.labels) + 2 * np.std(self.labels) print(f"Updated threshold: {self.threshold}") def get_service_name(id): with open('id.json', 'r') as f: id_mapping = json.load(f) return id_mapping.get(id) def access_service_folder(service_name): service_folder_path = f"./{service_name}" if os.path.exists(service_folder_path): return service_folder_path else: raise FileNotFoundError(f"Service folder for {service_name} not found.") def load_attributes(service_folder_path): attributes_file_path = os.path.join(service_folder_path, 'pateStandardDef3V1PointProcessedAttributes.txt') attributes = {} with open(attributes_file_path, 'r') as file: for line in file: key, value = line.strip().split('=') if key == 'Anomaly Labels': attributes[key] = [int(x) for x in value.strip('[]').split(',')] else: attributes[key] = float(value) if '.' in value else int(value) return attributes def save_attributes(service_folder_path, detector): attributes_file_path = os.path.join(service_folder_path, 'pateStandardDef3V1PointProcessedAttributes.txt') with open(attributes_file_path, 'w') as f: f.write(f"e_buffer={detector.e_buffer}\n") f.write(f"d_buffer={detector.d_buffer}\n") f.write(f"binary_scores={detector.binary_scores}\n") f.write(f"threshold={detector.threshold}\n") f.write(f"PATE Score (AUC-PR)={detector.result}\n") f.write(f"Anomaly Labels={detector.labels}\n") print(f"Attributes saved to {attributes_file_path}") def append_data_to_csv(service_folder_path, timestamp, value, is_anomaly): data_csv_path = os.path.join(service_folder_path, 'pateStandardDef3V1PointProcessedData.csv') if os.path.exists(data_csv_path): df = pd.read_csv(data_csv_path) else: # Create a new DataFrame if the file does not exist df = pd.DataFrame(columns=['reference_time', 'is_anomaly', 'usage_end_time', 'cost', 'usage_amount', 'usage_unit', 'service_type']) new_entry = { 'reference_time': (timestamp - pd.to_datetime(df['usage_end_time']).min()).total_seconds() / 3600 if not df.empty else 0, 'is_anomaly': is_anomaly, 'usage_end_time': timestamp, 'cost': value, 'usage_amount': None, # Update if necessary 'usage_unit': None, # Update if necessary 'service_type': None # Update if necessary } df = df.append(new_entry, ignore_index=True) df.to_csv(data_csv_path, index=False) print(f"New data appended and saved to {data_csv_path}") def CRADRM(received_id, value): # Step 1: Get service name and folder path service_name = get_service_name(received_id) service_folder_path = access_service_folder(service_name) # Step 2: Load existing attributes attrs = load_attributes(service_folder_path) # Initialize the detector with the loaded attributes detector = SyntheticLabelPATEAnomalyDetector( e_buffer=attrs['e_buffer'], d_buffer=attrs['d_buffer'], binary_scores=bool(attrs['binary_scores']), threshold=attrs['threshold'], result=attrs['PATE Score (AUC-PR)'], labels=attrs['Anomaly Labels'] ) # Step 3: Detect if the new value is an anomaly is_anomaly = detector.detect_single_anomaly(value) # Step 4: Update the model's attributes with the new data point detector.labels.append(is_anomaly) detector.update_model_attributes(value) # Step 5: Append the new data to the CSV timestamp = pd.Timestamp.now() # Assume current timestamp for the new data point append_data_to_csv(service_folder_path, timestamp, value, is_anomaly) # Step 6: Save the updated attributes to the .txt file save_attributes(service_folder_path, detector) # Example of how to use the function if __name__ == "__main__": # Example received_id and value to process received_id = "service123" value = 0.15 # Example value to be processed CRADRM(received_id, value) ``` ### Explanation of the Updated Code: 1. **`CRADRM(received_id, value)`**: - **Input**: This function now takes `received_id` and `value` as inputs, representing the service identifier and the new data value, respectively. - **Process**: - The service name is determined based on the `received_id`. - The service-specific folder is accessed to locate necessary files. - The model attributes are loaded from the `pateStandardDef3V1PointProcessedAttributes.txt` file. - The model determines if the new value is an anomaly. - The model attributes are updated based on the new data. - The new data, along with the anomaly label, is appended to the CSV file. - The updated model attributes are saved back to the text file. 2. **`append_data_to_csv()`**: - This function appends the new data point, along with its anomaly label, to the existing CSV file. 3. **`SyntheticLabelPATEAnomalyDetector` Class**: - Handles the detection of anomalies and updates the model's attributes accordingly. 4. **Usage**: - The function is called by passing the `received_id` and the new `value`. - The process is automated and will update all necessary files based on the received data. ### Integration: You can integrate this function into your server-side application where the `CRADRM(received_id, value)` will be triggered every time new data is received.ChatGPT
